As a result, Ian briefly transitioned into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical_storm" title="Subtropical storm">subtropical storm</a> around 18:00 UTC, but re-acquired tropical characteristics just 18 hours later while moving northeastward away from the aforementioned trough.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IanTCR_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-IanTCR-84">[82]</a></sup> By 06:00 UTC on September 16, a small mid-level eye became apparent and Ian began to intensify,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idisc16_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-idisc16-86">[84]</a></sup> with winds reaching 60 mph (95 km/h) at that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IanTCR_84-2"><a href="#cite_note-IanTCR-84">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idisc16_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-idisc16-86">[84]</a></sup> However, deep convection soon dissipated as cold air wrapped into the center, marking Ian's transition into an extratropical cyclone around 12:00 UTC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> On September 17, Ian's remnants were absorbed by a larger extratropical cyclone and soon dissipated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IanTCR_84-3"><a href="#cite_note-IanTCR-84">[82]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Julia">Tropical Storm Julia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Julia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Julia_2016-09-13_1825Z.jpg"><img alt="Julia 2016-09-13 1825Z.jpg" data-file-height="7800" data-file-width="6000" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Julia_2016-09-13_1825Z.jpg/150px-Julia_2016-09-13_1825Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Julia_2016-09-13_1825Z.jpg/225px-Julia_2016-09-13_1825Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Julia_2016-09-13_1825Z.jpg/300px-Julia_2016-09-13_1825Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Julia_2016_track.png"><img alt="Julia 2016 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Julia_2016_track.png/150px-Julia_2016_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Julia_2016_track.png/225px-Julia_2016_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Julia_2016_track.png/300px-Julia_2016_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 13 – September 18</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>50 mph (85 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1007 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Julia_(2016)" title="Tropical Storm Julia (2016)">Tropical Storm Julia (2016)</a></div>
<p>On September 1, a tropical wave entered the Atlantic from the west coast of Africa. A low pressure area developed after a burst in convection near the Leeward Islands around September 6, but dry air and wind shear inhibited further development. At 06:00 UTC on September 13, the system maintained sufficient organization to become a tropical depression. Around that time, it made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Jensen_Beach,_Florida" title="Jensen Beach, Florida">Jensen Beach, Florida</a>. Despite being inland, the depression intensified into Tropical Storm Julia over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacksonville" title="Jacksonville">Jacksonville</a> and peaked with winds of 50 mph (85 km/h) shortly thereafter. The cyclone drifted north-northwestward and then northeastward, moving offshore the Southeastern United States on September 14 under a weak steering regime. A cyclonic loop occurred as strong westerly air developed in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JuliaTCR_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-JuliaTCR-88">[86]</a></sup> The shear caused fluctuations in intensity, while there were bursts of convection around the disorganized center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> By September 19, the center of Julia was devoid of strong convection, as rainbands rapidly diminished, and soon degraded into a remnant low. The remnants dissipated over eastern North Carolina on September 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JuliaTCR_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-JuliaTCR-88">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Parts of North Carolina received as much as 12 in (300 mm) of rain, while as much as 18 in (460 mm) fell in the <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">Hampton Roads</a> area of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>. A total of 63 people had to be rescued from their homes, and 61 were evacuated from nursing homes. One million gallons of sewage from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_City" title="Elizabeth City">Elizabeth City</a> flowed into the <a href="/wiki/Pasquotank_River" title="Pasquotank River">Pasquotank River</a> and Charles Creek. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cashie_River" title="Cashie River">Cashie River</a> in <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_North_Carolina" title="Windsor, North Carolina">Windsor, North Carolina</a>, reached 15 ft (4.6 m) on September 22, 2 ft (0.61 m) above flood stage. That same day, <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_North_Carolina" title="Governor of North Carolina">Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Pat_McCrory" title="Pat McCrory">Pat McCrory</a> declared a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> in 11 counties. Schools were closed in <a href="/wiki/Bertie_County,_North_Carolina" title="Bertie County, North Carolina">Bertie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Currituck_County,_North_Carolina" title="Currituck County, North Carolina">Currituck</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hertford_County,_North_Carolina" title="Hertford County, North Carolina">Hertford</a> counties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Karl">Tropical Storm Karl</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Karl">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karl_2016-09-24_1450Z.jpg"><img alt="Karl 2016-09-24 1450Z.jpg" data-file-height="7200" data-file-width="5600" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Karl_2016-09-24_1450Z.jpg/150px-Karl_2016-09-24_1450Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Karl_2016-09-24_1450Z.jpg/225px-Karl_2016-09-24_1450Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Karl_2016-09-24_1450Z.jpg/300px-Karl_2016-09-24_1450Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karl_2016_track.png"><img alt="Karl 2016 track.png" data-file-height="2009" data-file-width="2700" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Karl_2016_track.png/150px-Karl_2016_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Karl_2016_track.png/225px-Karl_2016_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Karl_2016_track.png/300px-Karl_2016_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 14 – September 25</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>70 mph (110 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  988 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave emerged into the Atlantic from the west coast of Africa on September 12. The wave steadily organized while passing through the Cabo Verde Islands, and attained sufficient organization to be declared a tropical depression by 06:00 UTC on September 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KarlTCR_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-KarlTCR-91">[89]</a></sup> Strong shear plagued the cyclone, with its low-level circulation misplaced from the convection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> By 06:00 UTC on September 15, however, a significant burst of deep convection prompted the depression's upgrade to Tropical Storm Karl. The cyclone continued west for several days across the unfavorable central Atlantic, with convection sheared to the northeast and the circulation occasionally becoming poorly defined. Karl weakened to a tropical depression around 06:00 UTC on September 21 as it passed close to an upper-level low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KarlTCR_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-KarlTCR-91">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> However, by the following day, the upper-level low moved away to the south, causing a reduction in shear that allowed the system to reattain tropical storm intensity as it curved near Bermuda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KarlTCR_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-KarlTCR-91">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>On Bermuda, about 800 people lost power indirectly from the storm due to a mainline fault on the island.Otherwise, impacts on the island were relatively minimal. Sustained winds of 46 mph (74 km/h) and gusts to over 68 mph (109 km/h) were observed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KarlTCR_91-3"><a href="#cite_note-KarlTCR-91">[89]</a></sup> Along the east coast of the United States, long-period swells from Karl were recorded as it moved out to sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> Accelerating east-northeastwards, Karl continued to strengthen and it attained peak winds of 70 mph (110 km/h) early on September 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KarlTCR_91-4"><a href="#cite_note-KarlTCR-91">[89]</a></sup> However, cold air encroached on the low-level circulation by 12:00 UTC that day, marking Karl's transition to an extratropical cyclone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> Karl's remnant low continued northeast over the North Atlantic and was absorbed by another extratropical system early on September 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KarlTCR_91-5"><a href="#cite_note-KarlTCR-91">[89]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Lisa">Tropical Storm Lisa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Lisa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lisa_2016-09-21_1245Z.jpg"><img alt="Lisa 2016-09-21 1245Z.jpg" data-file-height="2104" data-file-width="1660" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Lisa_2016-09-21_1245Z.jpg/150px-Lisa_2016-09-21_1245Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Lisa_2016-09-21_1245Z.jpg/225px-Lisa_2016-09-21_1245Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Lisa_2016-09-21_1245Z.jpg/300px-Lisa_2016-09-21_1245Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lisa_2016_track.png"><img alt="Lisa 2016 track.png" data-file-height="1893" data-file-width="3000" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Lisa_2016_track.png/150px-Lisa_2016_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Lisa_2016_track.png/225px-Lisa_2016_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Lisa_2016_track.png/300px-Lisa_2016_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 19 – September 25</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>50 mph (85 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  999 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On September 14, the NHC noted the potential for tropical cyclone development in the East Atlantic later in the week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> A tropical wave moved off the west coast of Africa on September 16, developing into a tropical depression by 12:00 UTC on September 19, about 225 mi (360 km) west-southwest of the southernmost Cabo Verde Islands. On September 20, the depression strengthened to Tropical storm Lisa. Around 12:00 UTC on September 22, Lisa peaked with sustained winds of 50 mph (85 km/h) and a minimum pressure of 999 mbar (29.5 inHg). The storm soon began weakening due increasing wind shear, but Lisa briefly restrengthened on September 24. Lisa managed to maintain tropical storm intensity while battling unfavorable conditions until early on September 25, weakening to a tropical depression at that time. Lisa became a remnant low at 06:00 UTC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LisaTCR_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-LisaTCR-97">[95]</a></sup> The remnants were monitored for potential regeneration,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup> but failed to redevelop and dissipated later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LisaTCR_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-LisaTCR-97">[95]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Matthew">Hurricane Matthew</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Hurricane Matthew">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matthew_2016-09-30_1845Z.png"><img alt="Matthew 2016-09-30 1845Z.png" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1600" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Matthew_2016-09-30_1845Z.png/150px-Matthew_2016-09-30_1845Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Matthew_2016-09-30_1845Z.png/225px-Matthew_2016-09-30_1845Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Matthew_2016-09-30_1845Z.png/300px-Matthew_2016-09-30_1845Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matthew_2016_track.png"><img alt="Matthew 2016 track.png" data-file-height="2127" data-file-width="3000" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Matthew_2016_track.png/150px-Matthew_2016_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Matthew_2016_track.png/225px-Matthew_2016_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Matthew_2016_track.png/300px-Matthew_2016_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 28 – October 9</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>165 mph (270 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  934 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Matthew" title="Hurricane Matthew">Hurricane Matthew</a></div>
<p>A tropical wave developed into Tropical Storm Matthew near <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> on September 28. Continuing westward under the influence of a mid-level ridge, the storm steadily intensified to attain hurricane intensity by 18:00 UTC on September 29. The effects of southwesterly wind shear unexpectedly abated late that day, and Matthew began a period of rapid intensification; during a 24-hour period beginning at 00:00 UTC on September 30, the cyclone's maximum winds more than doubled, from 80 mph (130 km/h) to 165 mph (270 km/h), making Matthew a Category 5 hurricane,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthew_TCR_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew_TCR-30">[28]</a></sup> the first since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Felix" title="Hurricane Felix">Hurricane Felix</a> in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> Due to <a href="/wiki/Upwelling" title="Upwelling">upwelling</a> of cooler waters, Matthew weakened to a Category 4 hurricane later on October 1. Matthew remained a powerful Category 4 hurricane for several days, making landfall near <a href="/wiki/Les_Anglais" title="Les Anglais">Les Anglais</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, around 11:00 UTC on October 4 with winds of 150 mph (240 km/h). Continuing northward, the cyclone struck <a href="/wiki/Mais%C3%AD" title="Maisí">Maisí</a> in Cuba early on October 5. Cuba's and Haiti's mountainous terrain weakened Matthew to Category 3 status, as it began to accelerate northwestwards through <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthew_TCR_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew_TCR-30">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Restrengthening occurred as Matthew's circulation became better organized, with the storm becoming a Category 4 hurricane again while passing <a href="/wiki/Freeport,_Bahamas" title="Freeport, Bahamas">Freeport</a>. However, Matthew began to weaken again as an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a> took place. The storm significantly weakened while closely paralleling the coasts of Florida and Georgia, with the northwestern portion of the outer eyewall coming ashore in Florida while the system was a Category 3 hurricane. Matthew weakened to a Category 2 hurricane late on October 7 and then to a Category 1 hurricane by 12:00 UTC on October 8. About three hours later, the hurricane made landfall at <a href="/wiki/Cape_Romain_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Cape Romain National Wildlife Refuge">Cape Romain National Wildlife Refuge</a>, near <a href="/wiki/McClellanville,_South_Carolina" title="McClellanville, South Carolina">McClellanville, South Carolina</a>, with winds of 85 mph (140 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthew_TCR_30-3"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew_TCR-30">[28]</a></sup> Convection became displaced as Matthew pulled away from land,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHC-Matthew-ADV_47_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHC-Matthew-ADV_47-100">[98]</a></sup> with Matthew becoming extratropical about 200 mi (320 km) east of Cape Hatteras, North Carolina, on October 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthew_TCR_30-4"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew_TCR-30">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Heavy rains and strong winds buffeted the Lesser Antilles. The winds caused widespread power outages and damaged crops, particularly in St. Lucia, while flooding and landslides caused by the rainfall damaged many homes and roads. One person died in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(Antilles)" title="Saint Vincent (Antilles)">St. Vincent</a> when he was crushed by a boulder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> The storm brought precipitation to <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Guajira_Peninsula" title="Guajira Peninsula">Guajira Peninsula</a>, which saw its first heavy rain event in three years. One person drowned in a river in <a href="/wiki/Uribia,_La_Guajira" title="Uribia, La Guajira">Uribia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> In Haiti, flooding and high winds disrupted telecommunications and destroyed extensive swaths of land; around 80% of <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%A9mie" title="Jérémie">Jérémie</a> sustained significant damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103">[101]</a></sup> Matthew left about $1.9 billion in damage and at least 546 deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthew_TCR_30-5"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew_TCR-30">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedim_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-cedim-104">[102]</a></sup> Heavy rainfall spread eastward across the Dominican Republic, where four were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DR_Deaths_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-DR_Deaths-105">[103]</a></sup> Effects in Cuba were most severe along the coast, where storm surge caused extensive damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> Four people were killed due to a bridge collapse,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BNO_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-BNO-107">[105]</a></sup> and total losses in the country amounted to $2.58 billion, most of which occurred in the <a href="/wiki/Guant%C3%A1namo_Province" title="Guantánamo Province">Guantánamo Province</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_China_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_China-108">[106]</a></sup> Passing through the Bahamas as a major hurricane, Matthew inflicted severe impacts across several islands, particularly Grand Bahama, where an estimated 95% of homes sustained damage in the townships of Eight Mile Rock and Holmes Rock. In Florida, much of the damage occurred was caused by strong winds and storm surge in the east-central and northeastern portions of the state. About 1.2 million people lost power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthew_TCR_30-6"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew_TCR-30">[28]</a></sup> Damage in Florida reached over $2.75 billion and there were 12 deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> An additional 1.3 million people lost electricity in Georgia and South Carolina combined. Torrential rain caused severe flooding, especially in North Carolina and South Carolina,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthew_TCR_30-7"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew_TCR-30">[28]</a></sup> where some rivers exceed record heights set by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Floyd" title="Hurricane Floyd">Hurricane Floyd</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">1928 Okeechobee hurricane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthew_TCR_30-8"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew_TCR-30">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> In North Carolina, 100,000 structures were flooded and damage reached $1.5 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthew_TCR_30-9"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew_TCR-30">[28]</a></sup> Overall, Matthew caused at least 603 deaths and about $15.1 billion in damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthew_TCR_30-10"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew_TCR-30">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BNO_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-BNO-107">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Nicole">Hurricane Nicole</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Hurricane Nicole">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicole_2016-10-13_0555Z.jpg"><img alt="Nicole 2016-10-13 0555Z.jpg" data-file-height="3848" data-file-width="2736" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Nicole_2016-10-13_0555Z.jpg/150px-Nicole_2016-10-13_0555Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Nicole_2016-10-13_0555Z.jpg/225px-Nicole_2016-10-13_0555Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Nicole_2016-10-13_0555Z.jpg/300px-Nicole_2016-10-13_0555Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicole_2016_track.png"><img alt="Nicole 2016 track.png" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="3000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Nicole_2016_track.png/150px-Nicole_2016_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Nicole_2016_track.png/225px-Nicole_2016_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Nicole_2016_track.png/300px-Nicole_2016_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 4 – October 18</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>140 mph (220 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  950 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Nicole_(2016)" title="Hurricane Nicole (2016)">Hurricane Nicole (2016)</a></div>
<p>A tropical wave developed into Tropical Storm Nicole about 530 mi (850 km) northeast of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan, Puerto Rico</a>, early on October 4, <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NicoleTCR_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-NicoleTCR-31">[29]</a></sup> based on an ASCAT pass revealing a well-defined surface circulation and winds of up to 50 mph (85 km/h). The NHC forecast only gradual strengthening as the storm moved slowly to the north due to weak steering currents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> An eye then became visible at both mid- and upper-level heights, and Nicole <a href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">rapidly strengthened</a> to a Category 2 hurricane to the south of <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>, as winds reached 105 mph (165 km/h) early on October 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NicoleTCR_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-NicoleTCR-31">[29]</a></sup> With Matthew located offshore Florida, this was the first time since <a href="/wiki/1964_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1964 Atlantic hurricane season">1964</a> that two hurricanes at or above Category 2 existed simultaneously in the western Atlantic Ocean (65°W).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cat2_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-cat2-114">[112]</a></sup> However, Nicole was then impacted by wind shear, with the eye soon becoming no longer visible and convection diminishing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> Nicole rapidly weakened to a strong tropical storm on October 7. Further weakening occurred as it drifted southward, and by October 8, the circulation was exposed and the system was barely a tropical storm, with all convection displaced to the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> Later that day, an impressive burst of convection flared up over the center, and Nicole again became more organized as it began to turn to the north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gradual intensification continued throughout the next few days before briefly stopping, then later resuming on October 11 as the storm turned towards Bermuda and re-strengthened to Category 1 status. On October 12, Nicole became a Category 2 hurricane again. Later on the same day, Nicole became a major hurricane upon reaching Category 3 intensity. The next day, Nicole briefly strengthened into a Category 4 hurricane, peaking with maximum sustained winds of 140 mph (220 km/h). However, the storm weakened back to a Category 3 hurricane several hours later due to increasing vertical wind shear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NicoleTCR_31-3"><a href="#cite_note-NicoleTCR-31">[29]</a></sup> At 15:00 UTC on October 13, the hurricane's eye passed directly over Bermuda, where <a href="/wiki/Automated_airport_weather_station#Automated_Surface_Observing_System_.28ASOS.29" title="Automated airport weather station">automated surface station</a> measured sustained winds of 87 mph (141 km/h) and a gust reaching 119 mph (191 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> At 06:00 UTC on October 14, southwesterly wind shear reduced the system to Category 1 status. The storm slowly began to weaken the next day, falling to a tropical storm intensity early on October 18. Nicole transitioned into an extratropical cyclone at 06:00 UTC later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NicoleTCR_31-4"><a href="#cite_note-NicoleTCR-31">[29]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Otto">Hurricane Otto</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Hurricane Otto">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Otto_2016-11-24_1605Z.jpg"><img alt="Otto 2016-11-24 1605Z.jpg" data-file-height="6800" data-file-width="5100" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Otto_2016-11-24_1605Z.jpg/150px-Otto_2016-11-24_1605Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Otto_2016-11-24_1605Z.jpg/225px-Otto_2016-11-24_1605Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Otto_2016-11-24_1605Z.jpg/300px-Otto_2016-11-24_1605Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Otto_2016_track.png"><img alt="Otto 2016 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Otto_2016_track.png/150px-Otto_2016_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Otto_2016_track.png/225px-Otto_2016_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Otto_2016_track.png/300px-Otto_2016_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>November 20 – November 25<br/>
<small>(<a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_hurricane_season#Tropical_Storm_Otto" title="2016 Pacific hurricane season">Exited basin</a>)</small></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>115 mph (185 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  975 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Otto" title="Hurricane Otto">Hurricane Otto</a></div>
<p>On November 15, a broad low pressure area developed in the southwestern Caribbean Sea. After an increase in convective organization, the system developed into a tropical depression about 120 mi (190 km) north of <a href="/wiki/Col%C3%B3n,_Panama" title="Colón, Panama">Colón, Panama</a> late on November 20. Fueled by warm waters and good outflow, the depression intensified into Tropical Storm Otto by 06:00 UTC on November 21. Otto deepened into a hurricane on November 23 while drifting westward; this was the latest date for a tropical cyclone to reach that intensity over the Caribbean Sea, one day later than the previous record set by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Martha" title="Hurricane Martha">Hurricane Martha</a> in 1969. Otto rapidly intensified throughout the following day, and at 17:30 UTC November 24, the storm made landfall on the southern <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> coast near <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_de_Nicaragua" title="San Juan de Nicaragua">San Juan de Nicaragua</a> at peak intensity, as a Category 3 major hurricane with winds of 115 mph (185 km/h). This was the southernmost hurricane landfall in <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>. Weakening ensued as Otto moved inland. Around 03:30 UTC on November 25, Otto exited into <a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_hurricane_season#Tropical_Storm_Otto" title="2016 Pacific hurricane season">the Eastern Pacific</a>, marking the first time a tropical cyclone survived the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Atlantic%E2%80%93Pacific_crossover_hurricanes" title="List of Atlantic–Pacific crossover hurricanes">crossover from the Atlantic to the Eastern Pacific</a> since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Cesar%E2%80%93Douglas" title="Hurricane Cesar–Douglas">Hurricane Cesar–Douglas</a> in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otto_TCR_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Otto_TCR-119">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, the outerbands of Otto brought heavy precipitation and strong winds. The hurricane left nine deaths in the country, with one after a house was struck by a falling tree in <a href="/wiki/Panama_City" title="Panama City">Panama City</a>, three from landslides, two by drowning in a rain-swollen river, and three others after the ship <i>Jessica</i> sank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> Generally, rainfall of 3 to 6 in (76 to 152 mm) was observed in <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otto_TCR_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-Otto_TCR-119">[117]</a></sup> Throughout the country, Otto damaged 857 houses, 8 schools, and 2 health facilities. About 5,600 ft (1,700 m) of power lines were damaged, causing power and water outages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocha1129_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-ocha1129-121">[119]</a></sup> Four deaths were reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, rainfall peaked at 12.11 in (308 mm) at <a href="/wiki/Miravalles_Volcano" title="Miravalles Volcano">Miravalles Volcano</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otto_TCR_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-Otto_TCR-119">[117]</a></sup> Flooding and mudslides left 42 communities isolated and damaged 14 water systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocha1129_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-ocha1129-121">[119]</a></sup> Damage reached at least $190 million and there were 10 fatalities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otto_TCR_119-3"><a href="#cite_note-Otto_TCR-119">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otto_damage_total_-_BN_Americas_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Otto_damage_total_-_BN_Americas-123">[121]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_system">Other system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bay_of_Biscay_cyclone_2016-09-15.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="371" data-file-width="615" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Bay_of_Biscay_cyclone_2016-09-15.png/220px-Bay_of_Biscay_cyclone_2016-09-15.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Bay_of_Biscay_cyclone_2016-09-15.png/330px-Bay_of_Biscay_cyclone_2016-09-15.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Bay_of_Biscay_cyclone_2016-09-15.png/440px-Bay_of_Biscay_cyclone_2016-09-15.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bay_of_Biscay_cyclone_2016-09-15.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The cyclone on September 15</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On September 15, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9t%C3%A9o-France" title="Météo-France">Météo-France</a> began monitoring a cyclone in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a> that they claimed was <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_cyclone" title="Subtropical cyclone">subtropical</a>, having apparently possessing an asymmetric wind field of tropical-storm force winds and a warm thermal core.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoBCycloneStats1_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-BoBCycloneStats1-124">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> However, American meteorological agencies disagreed and determined it was non-tropical,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WU_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-WU-126">[124]</a></sup> as proven by surface analysis data from NOAA, which showed that the cyclone still had an <a href="/wiki/Occluded_front" title="Occluded front">occluded front</a> connected to it – signs that usually indicate an extratropical cyclone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frontal_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-frontal-127">[125]</a></sup> The system drifted southeastwards, attaining a peak intensity of 996 mbar (29.4 inHg),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoBCycloneStats1_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-BoBCycloneStats1-124">[122]</a></sup> and eventually made landfall near the border of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, rapidly weakening and eventually dissipating shortly thereafter, early on September 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-m60_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-m60-128">[126]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Free_University_of_Berlin" title="Free University of Berlin">Free University of Berlin</a>, in accordance with their naming of cyclones that affect their area, named the cyclone "Stephanie".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kugel_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-kugel-129">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>The cyclone brought only minor damage to Spain and France, most of which were caused by some strong wind gusts, swells, and some heavy rainfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kugel_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-kugel-129">[127]</a></sup> Maximum gusts of up to 81 mph (130 km/h) were reported on the coast of <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Basque Country</a>, with slightly higher gusts in the upper elevations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-impact_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-impact-130">[128]</a></sup> A storm surge of 3–4 ft (0.91–1.22 m) was also reported on the coastlines of Spain and France. No major damage, fatalities or injuries were reported as a result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-impact_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-impact-130">[128]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storm_names">Storm names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Storm names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">Tropical cyclone naming</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_tropical_cyclone_naming" title="History of tropical cyclone naming">History of tropical cyclone naming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names" title="List of historic tropical cyclone names">List of historic tropical cyclone names</a></div>
<p>The following <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">list of names</a> was used for named storms that formed in the North Atlantic in 2016. The names not retired from this list will be used again in the 2022 season. This was the same list used in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2010 Atlantic hurricane season">2010 season</a>, with the exception of Ian and Tobias, which replaced <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Igor" title="Hurricane Igor">Igor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Tomas" title="Hurricane Tomas">Tomas</a>, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retired_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-retired-131">[129]</a></sup> The name Ian was used for the first time this year.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Atlantic_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Atlantic hurricane names">List of retired Atlantic hurricane names</a></div>
<p>On March 26, 2017, at the 39th session of the RA IV hurricane committee, the World Meteorological Organization retired the names <i>Matthew</i> and <i>Otto</i> from its rotating name lists due to the amount of damage and deaths they caused, and they will not be used again for another <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane" title="Atlantic hurricane">Atlantic hurricane</a>. They will be replaced with <i>Martin</i> and <i>Owen</i> for the 2022 season, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_effects">Season effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Season effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This is a table of all the storms that formed in the 2016 Atlantic hurricane season. It includes their duration, names, landfall(s), denoted in parentheses, damages, and death totals. Deaths in parentheses are additional and indirect (an example of an indirect death would be a traffic accident), but were still related to that storm. Damage and deaths include totals while the storm was extratropical, a wave, or a low, and all the damage figures are in 2016 USD.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-Otto-note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Otto-note_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The last storm, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Otto" title="Hurricane Otto">Otto</a>, did not dissipate on November 25. It crossed into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Pacific" title="Eastern Pacific">Eastern Pacific</a>, and because it was the final storm of the season, the crossover date is listed on here as the dissipation date.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-damage-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-damage_2-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">All damage figures are in 2016 <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>, unless otherwise noted</span></li>
</ol>
